<div class="noprint" id="mw-head-base">\n  </div>\n  <div class="mw-body" id="content" role="main">\n   <a id="top">\n   </a>\n   <div class="mw-body-content" id="siteNotice">\n    <!-- CentralNotice -->\n   </div>\n   <div class="mw-indicators mw-body-content">\n   </div>\n   <h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">\n    Astrobiology\n   </h1>\n   <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">\n    <div class="noprint" id="siteSub">\n     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia\n    </div>\n    <div id="contentSub">\n    </div>\n    <div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">\n     Jump to:\n     <a href="#mw-head">\n      navigation\n     </a>\n     ,\n     <a href="#p-search">\n      search\n     </a>\n    </div>\n    <div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en">\n     <div class="mw-parser-output">\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       "Exobiology" redirects here. It is not to be confused with\n       <a href="/wiki/Xenobiology" title="Xenobiology">\n        Xenobiology\n       </a>\n       .\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Abiogenesis" title="Abiogenesis">\n        Abiogenesis\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Earliest_known_life_forms" title="Earliest known life forms">\n        Earliest known life forms\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Panspermia" title="Panspermia">\n        Panspermia\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Further information:\n       <a href="/wiki/Astrobiology_(journal)" title="Astrobiology (journal)">\n        Astrobiology (journal)\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Astrobiology_Magazine" title="Astrobiology Magazine">\n        Astrobiology Magazine\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:183px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ADN_animation.gif">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="313" data-file-width="181" height="313" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/81/ADN_animation.gif" width="181"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ADN_animation.gif" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nucleic_acids" title="Nucleic acids">\n          Nucleic acids\n         </a>\n         may not be the only\n         <a href="/wiki/Biomolecule" title="Biomolecule">\n          biomolecules\n         </a>\n         in the Universe capable of coding for life processes.\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AstroDNA_1-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-AstroDNA-1">\n           [1]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       <b>\n        Astrobiology\n       </b>\n       is the study of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Abiogenesis" title="Abiogenesis">\n        origin\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Evolution" title="Evolution">\n        evolution\n       </a>\n       , distribution, and future of\n       <a href="/wiki/Life" title="Life">\n        life\n       </a>\n       in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Universe" title="Universe">\n        universe\n       </a>\n       :\n       <a href="/wiki/Extraterrestrial_life" title="Extraterrestrial life">\n        extraterrestrial life\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Earliest_known_life_forms" title="Earliest known life forms">\n        life on Earth\n       </a>\n       . Astrobiology addresses the question of whether life exists beyond Earth, and how humans can detect it if it does.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-about_2-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-about-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The term\n       <b>\n        exobiology\n       </b>\n       is similar but more specific\xe2\x80\x94it covers the search for life beyond Earth, and the effects of extraterrestrial environments on living things.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Astrobiology makes use of\n       <a href="/wiki/Physics" title="Physics">\n        physics\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Chemistry" title="Chemistry">\n        chemistry\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Astronomy" title="Astronomy">\n        astronomy\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Biology" title="Biology">\n        biology\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Molecular_biology" title="Molecular biology">\n        molecular biology\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Ecology" title="Ecology">\n        ecology\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Planetary_science" title="Planetary science">\n        planetary science\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Geography" title="Geography">\n        geography\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Geology" title="Geology">\n        geology\n       </a>\n       to investigate the possibility of life on other worlds and help recognize\n       <a href="/wiki/Biosphere" title="Biosphere">\n        biospheres\n       </a>\n       that might be different from that on Earth.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-4">\n         [4]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Abiogenesis" title="Abiogenesis">\n        The origin\n       </a>\n       and early evolution of life is an inseparable part of the discipline of astrobiology.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Astrobiology concerns itself with interpretation of existing\n       <a href="/wiki/Scientific_method" title="Scientific method">\n        scientific data\n       </a>\n       , and although speculation is entertained to give context, astrobiology concerns itself primarily with\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hypotheses" title="Hypotheses">\n        hypotheses\n       </a>\n       that fit firmly into existing\n       <a href="/wiki/Theory#Science" title="Theory">\n        scientific theories\n       </a>\n       . Given more detailed and reliable data from other parts of the universe, the roots of astrobiology itself\xe2\x80\x94physics, chemistry and biology\xe2\x80\x94may have their theoretical bases challenged.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       This\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interdisciplinary" title="Interdisciplinary">\n        interdisciplinary\n       </a>\n       field encompasses research on the origin and evolution of\n       <a href="/wiki/Planetary_system" title="Planetary system">\n        planetary systems\n       </a>\n       , origins of\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_interstellar_and_circumstellar_molecules" title="List of interstellar and circumstellar molecules">\n        organic compounds in space\n       </a>\n       , rock-water-carbon interactions,\n       <a href="/wiki/Abiogenesis" title="Abiogenesis">\n        abiogenesis\n       </a>\n       on Earth,\n       <a href="/wiki/Planetary_habitability" title="Planetary habitability">\n        planetary habitability\n       </a>\n       , research on\n       <a href="/wiki/Biosignature" title="Biosignature">\n        biosignatures\n       </a>\n       for life detection, and studies on the potential for life to adapt to challenges on Earth and in\n       <a href="/wiki/Outer_space" title="Outer space">\n        outer space\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Goals2016_6-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Goals2016-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-20151218-jc_7-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NYT-20151218-jc-7">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">\n        <a href="#cite_note-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Biochemistry" title="Biochemistry">\n        chemistry of life\n       </a>\n       may have begun shortly after the\n       <a href="/wiki/Big_Bang" title="Big Bang">\n        Big Bang\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Age_of_the_universe" title="Age of the universe">\n        13.8 billion years ago\n       </a>\n       , during a habitable epoch when the\n       <a href="/wiki/Universe" title="Universe">\n        Universe\n       </a>\n       was only 10\xe2\x80\x9317 million years old.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IJA-2014October_9-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-IJA-2014October-9">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ARXIV-20131202_10-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ARXIV-20131202-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-20141202_11-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NYT-20141202-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       According to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Panspermia" title="Panspermia">\n        panspermia\n       </a>\n       hypothesis, microscopic life\xe2\x80\x94distributed by\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Meteoroids" title="Meteoroids">\n        meteoroids\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Asteroid" title="Asteroid">\n        asteroids\n       </a>\n       and other\n       <a href="/wiki/Small_Solar_System_body" title="Small Solar System body">\n        small Solar System bodies\n       </a>\n       \xe2\x80\x94may exist throughout the universe.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USRA-2010_12-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-USRA-2010-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       According to research published in August 2015, very large galaxies may be more favorable to the creation and development of\n       <a href="/wiki/Planetary_habitability" title="Planetary habitability">\n        habitable planets\n       </a>\n       than such smaller galaxies as the\n       <a href="/wiki/Milky_Way" title="Milky Way">\n        Milky Way\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SP-20150821_13-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-SP-20150821-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Nonetheless, Earth is the only place in the universe humans know to harbor life.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA-1990_14-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NASA-1990-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Astrobiology-2008_15-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Astrobiology-2008-15">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Estimates of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Habitable_zone" title="Habitable zone">\n        habitable zones\n       </a>\n       around other stars,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">\n        <a href="#cite_note-16">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-20131118_17-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NYT-20131118-17">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       sometimes referred to as "Goldilocks zones," along with the discovery of hundreds of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extrasolar_planet" title="Extrasolar planet">\n        extrasolar planets\n       </a>\n       and new insights into extreme habitats here on Earth, suggest that there may be many more habitable places in the universe than considered possible until very recently.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-20131104_18-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NYT-20131104-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PNAS-20131031_19-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-PNAS-20131031-19">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LATimes-20131104_20-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-LATimes-20131104-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Mars_Science_Laboratory#Current_status" title="Timeline of Mars Science Laboratory">\n        Current studies\n       </a>\n       on the planet\n       <a href="/wiki/Mars" title="Mars">\n        Mars\n       </a>\n       by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Curiosity_(rover)" title="Curiosity (rover)">\n        <i>\n         Curiosity\n        </i>\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Opportunity_(rover)" title="Opportunity (rover)">\n        <i>\n         Opportunity\n        </i>\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Mars_rover" title="Mars rover">\n        rovers\n       </a>\n       are searching for evidence of ancient life as well as plains related to ancient rivers or lakes that may have been\n       <a href="/wiki/Planetary_habitability" title="Planetary habitability">\n        habitable\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SCI-20140124a_21-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-SCI-20140124a-21">\n         [21]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SCI-20140124special_22-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-SCI-20140124special-22">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SCI-20140124_23-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-SCI-20140124-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SCI-20140124c_24-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-SCI-20140124c-24">\n         [24]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The search for evidence of\n       <a href="/wiki/Planetary_habitability" title="Planetary habitability">\n        habitability\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Taphonomy" title="Taphonomy">\n        taphonomy\n       </a>\n       (related to\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fossils" title="Fossils">\n        fossils\n       </a>\n       ), and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Organic_molecule" title="Organic molecule">\n        organic molecules\n       </a>\n       on the planet Mars is now a primary\n       <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">\n        NASA\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ESA" title="ESA">\n        ESA\n       </a>\n       objective.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <div class="toc" id="toc">\n       <div class="toctitle">\n        <h2>\n         Contents\n        </h2>\n       </div>\n       <ul>\n        <li class="toclevel-1        <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-8">\n             <a href="#Astroecology">\n              <span class="tocnumber">\n               2.3.3\n              </span>\n              <span           <span class="tocnumber">\n               2.3.4\n              </span>\n              <span class="toctext">\n               Astrogeology\n              </span>\n             </a>\n            </li>\n           </ul>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-10">\n         <a href="#Life_in_the_Solar_System">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           3\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Life in the Solar System\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-11">\n         <a href="#Rare_Earth_hypothesis">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           4\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Rare Earth hypothesis\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-12">\n         <a href="#Research">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           5\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Research\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-13">\n           <a     </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-14">\n         <a href="#Missions">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           6\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Missions\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-15">\n           <a href="#Viking_program">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             6.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Viking program\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-16">\n           <a href="#Beagle_2">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             6.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Beagle 2\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-17">\n           <a href="#EXPOSE">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             6.3\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             EXPOSE\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-18">\n           <a href="#Mars_Science_Laboratory">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             6.4\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Mars Science Laboratory\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-19">\n           <a href="#Tanpopo">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             6.5\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Tanpopo\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-20">\n           <a href="#ExoMars_rover">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             6.6\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             ExoMars rover\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-21">\n           <a href="#Mars_2020">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             6.7\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Mars 2020\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-22">\n           <a href="#Europa_Clipper">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             6.8\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Europa Clipper\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-23">\n           <a href="#Proposed_concepts">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             6.9\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Proposed concepts\n            </span>\n           </a>\n           <ul>\n            <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-24">\n             <a href="#Icebreaker_Life">\n              <span class="tocnumber">\n               6.9.1\n              </span>\n              <span class="toctext">\n               Icebreaker Life\n              </span>\n             </a>\n            </li>\n            <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-25">\n             <a href="#Journey_to_Enceladus_and_Titan">\n              <span class="tocnumber">\n               6.9.2\n              </span>\n              <span class="toctext">\n               Journey to Enceladus and Titan\n              </span>\n             </a>\n            </li>\n            <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-26">\n             <a href="#Enceladus_Life_Finder">\n              <span class="tocnumber">\n               6.9.3\n              </span>\n              <span class="toctext">\n               Enceladus Life Finder\n              </span>\n             </a>\n            </li>\n            <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-27">\n             <a href="#Life_Investigation_For_Enceladus">\n              <span class="tocnumber">\n               6.9.4\n              </span>\n              <span class="toctext">\n               Life Investigation For Enceladus\n              </span>\n             </a>\n            </li>\n            <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-28">\n             <a href="#Oceanus">\n              <span class="tocnumber">\n               6.9.5\n              </span>\n              <span class="toctext">\n               Oceanus\n              </span>\n             </a>\n            </li>\n            <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-29">\n             <a href="#Explorer_of_Enceladus_and_Titan">\n              <span class="tocnumber">\n               6.9.6\n              </span>\n              <span class="toctext">\n               Explorer of Enceladus and Titan\n              </span>\n             </a>\n            </li>\n           </ul>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-30">\n         <a href="#See_also">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           7\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           See also\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-31">\n         <a href="#References">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           8\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           References\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-32">\n         <a href="#Bibliography">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           9\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Bibliography\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-33">\n         <a href="#Further_reading">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           10\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Further reading\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-34">\n         <a href="#External_links">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           11\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           External links\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n       </ul>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Overview">\n        Overview\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Astrobiology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Overview">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       The term was first proposed by the Russian (\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soviet" title="Soviet">\n        Soviet\n       </a>\n       ) astronomer\n       <a href="/wiki/Gavriil_Adrianovich_Tikhov" title="Gavriil Adrianovich Tikhov">\n        Gavriil Tikhov\n       </a>\n       in 1953.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">\n        <a href="#cite_note-25">\n         [25]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <i>\n        Astrobiology\n       </i>\n       is etymologically derived from the\n       <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek" title="Ancient Greek">\n        Greek\n       </a>\n       <span lang="grc" xml:lang="grc">\n        \xe1\xbc\x84\xcf\x83\xcf\x84\xcf\x81\xce\xbf\xce\xbd\n       </span>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        astron\n       </i>\n       , "constellation, star";\n       <span lang="grc" xml:lang="grc">\n        \xce\xb2\xce\xaf\xce\xbf\xcf\x82\n       </span>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        bios\n       </i>\n       , "life"; and\n       <span lang="grc" xml:lang="grc">\n        -\xce\xbb\xce\xbf\xce\xb3\xce\xaf\xce\xb1\n       </span>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/-logia" title="wiktionary:-logia">\n         -logia\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        study\n       </i>\n       . The synonyms of astrobiology are diverse; however, the synonyms were structured in relation to the most important sciences implied in its development:\n       <a href="/wiki/Astronomy" title="Astronomy">\n        astronomy\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Biology" title="Biology">\n        biology\n       </a>\n       . A close synonym is\n       <i>\n        exobiology\n       </i>\n       from the Greek\n       <span lang="grc" xml:lang="grc">\n        \xce\x88\xce\xbe\xcf\x89\n       </span>\n       , "external"; \xce\x92\xce\xaf\xce\xbf\xcf\x82,\n       <i>\n        bios\n       </i>\n       , "life"; and \xce\xbb\xce\xbf\xce\xb3\xce\xaf\xce\xb1, -logia,\n       <i>\n        study\n       </i>\n       . The term exobiology was coined by molecular biologist\n       <a href="/wiki/Joshua_Lederberg" title="Joshua Lederberg">\n        Joshua Lederberg\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">\n        <a href="#cite_note-26">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Exobiology is considered to have a narrow scope limited to search of life external to Earth, whereas subject area of astrobiology is wider and investigates the link between life and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Universe" title="Universe">\n        universe\n       </a>\n       , which includes the search for extraterrestrial life, but also includes the study of life on Earth, its origin, evolution and limits.\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Plagiomnium_affine_laminazellen.jpeg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Plagiomnium_affine_laminazellen.jpeg/200px-Plagiomnium_affine_laminazellen.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Plagiomnium_affine_laminazellen.jpeg/300px-Plagiomnium_affine_laminazellen.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Plagiomnium_affine_laminazellen.jpeg/400px-Plagiomnium_affine_laminazellen.jpeg 2x" width="200"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Plagiomnium_affine_laminazellen.jpeg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         It is not known whether life elsewhere in the universe would utilize cell structures like those found on Earth. (\n         <a href="/wiki/Chloroplast" title="Chloroplast">\n          Chloroplasts\n         </a>\n         within plant cells shown here.)\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">\n          <a href="#cite_note-27">\n           [27]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Another term used in the past is\n       <a href="/wiki/Xenobiology" title="Xenobiology">\n        xenobiology\n       </a>\n       , ("biology of the foreigners") a word used in 1954 by science fiction writer\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Robert_Heinlein" title="Robert Heinlein">\n        Robert Heinlein\n       </a>\n       in his work\n       <a href="/wiki/The_Star_Beast" title="The Star Beast">\n        The Star Beast\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">\n        <a href="#cite_note-28">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The term xenobiology is now used in a more specialized sense, to mean "biology based on foreign chemistry", whether of extraterrestrial or terrestrial (possibly synthetic) origin. Since alternate chemistry analogs to some life-processes have been created in the laboratory, xenobiology is now considered as an extant subject.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">\n        <a href="#cite_note-29">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       While it is an emerging and developing field, the question of whether\n       <a href="/wiki/Life" title="Life">\n        life\n       </a>\n       exists elsewhere in the universe is a verifiable hypothesis and thus a valid line of\n       <a href="/wiki/Science" title="Science">\n        scientific\n       </a>\n       inquiry.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NAT-20170216_30-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NAT-20170216-30">\n         [30]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-20170215_31-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NYT-20170215-31">\n         [31]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Though once considered outside the mainstream of scientific inquiry, astrobiology has become a formalized field of study. Planetary scientist\n       <a href="/wiki/David_Grinspoon" title="David Grinspoon">\n        David Grinspoon\n       </a>\n       calls astrobiology a field of natural philosophy, grounding speculation on the unknown, in known scientific theory.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">\n        <a href="#cite_note-32">\n         [32]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       NASA\'s interest in exobiology first began with the development of the U.S. Space Program. In 1959, NASA funded its first exobiology project, and in 1960, NASA founded an Exobiology Program, which is now one of four main elements of NASA\'s current Astrobiology Program.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-about_2-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-about-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">\n        <a href="#cite_note-33">\n         [33]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In 1971, NASA funded the\n       <a href="/wiki/Search_for_extraterrestrial_intelligence" title="Search for extraterrestrial intelligence">\n        search for extraterrestrial intelligence\n       </a>\n       (SETI) to search radio frequencies of the electromagnetic spectrum for\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstellar_communication" title="Interstellar communication">\n        interstellar communications\n       </a>\n       transmitted by\n       <a href="/wiki/Extraterrestrial_life" title="Extraterrestrial life">\n        extraterrestrial life\n       </a>\n       outside the Solar System. NASA\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Viking_program" title="Viking program">\n        Viking missions\n       </a>\n       to Mars, launched in 1976, included\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Viking_biological_experiments" title="Viking biological experiments">\n        three biology experiments\n       </a>\n       designed to look for\n       <a href="/wiki/Metabolism" title="Metabolism">\n        metabolism\n       </a>\n       of present\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Life_on_Mars_(planet)" title="Life on Mars (planet)">\n        life on Mars\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2014_June_Astrobiology_and_Theology_seminer_01.JPG">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="4912" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/2014_June_Astrobiology_and_Theology_seminer_01.JPG/200px-2014_June_Astrobiology_and_Theology_seminer_01.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/2014_June_Astrobiology_and_Theology_seminer_01.JPG/300px-2014_June_Astrobiology_and_Theology_seminer_01.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/2014_June_Astrobiology_and_Theology_seminer_01.JPG/400px-2014_June_Astrobiology_and_Theology_seminer_01.JPG 2x" width="200"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2014_June_Astrobiology_and_Theology_seminer_01.JPG" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         In June 2014, the John W. Kluge Center of the Library of Congress held a seminar focusing on astrobiology. Panel members (L to R) Robin Lovin, Derek Malone-France, and\n         <a href="/wiki/Steven_J._Dick" title="Steven J. Dick">\n          Steven J. Dick\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Advancements in the fields of astrobiology, observational astronomy and discovery of large varieties of\n       <a href="/wiki/Extremophile" title="Extremophile">\n        extremophiles\n       </a>\n       with extraordinary capability to thrive in the harshest environments on Earth, have led to speculation that life may possibly be thriving on many of the extraterrestrial bodies in the universe. A particular focus of current astrobiology research is the search for\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Life_on_Mars_(planet)" title="Life on Mars (planet)">\n        life on Mars\n       </a>\n       due to this planet\'s proximity to Earth and geological history. There is a growing body of evidence to suggest that Mars has previously had a considerable amount of\n       <a href="/wiki/Water_on_Mars" title="Water on Mars">\n        water on its surface\n       </a>\n       , water being considered an essential precursor to the development of carbon-based life.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_34-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-34">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Missions specifically designed to search for current life on Mars were the\n       <a href="/wiki/Viking_program" title="Viking program">\n        Viking program\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Beagle_2" title="Beagle 2">\n        Beagle 2\n       </a>\n       probes. The Viking results were inconclusive,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">\n        <a href="#cite_note-35">\n         [35]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and Beagle 2 failed minutes after landing.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_News_16_Jan_2015_36-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-BBC_News_16_Jan_2015-36">\n         [36]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A future mission with a strong astrobiology role would have been the\n       <a href="/wiki/Jupiter_Icy_Moons_Orbiter" title="Jupiter Icy Moons Orbiter">\n        Jupiter Icy Moons Orbiter\n       </a>\n       , designed to study the frozen moons of Jupiter\xe2\x80\x94some of which may have liquid water\xe2\x80\x94had it not been cancelled. In late 2008, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Phoenix_(spacecraft)" title="Phoenix (spacecraft)">\n        Phoenix lander\n       </a>\n       probed the environment for past and present\n       <a href="/wiki/Planetary_habitability" title="Planetary habitability">\n        planetary habitability\n       </a>\n       of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Microbe" title="Microbe">\n        microbial\n       </a>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Life_on_Mars_(planet)" title="Life on Mars (planet)">\n        life on Mars\n       </a>\n       , and researched the history of water there.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In November 2011, NASA launched the\n       <a href="/wiki/Mars_Science_Laboratory" title="Mars Science Laboratory">\n        Mars Science Laboratory\n       </a>\n       mission carrying the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Curiosity_rover" title="Curiosity rover">\n        <i>\n         Curiosity\n        </i>\n       </a>\n       rover, which\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Curiosity_rover#Landing" title="Curiosity rover">\n        landed\n       </a>\n       on Mars at\n       <a href="/wiki/Gale_(crater)" title="Gale (crater)">\n        Gale Crater\n       </a>\n       in August 2012.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gale_Crater_37-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Gale_Crater-37">\n         [37]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gale_Crater2_38-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Gale_Crater2-38">\n         [38]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gale_Crater3_39-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Gale_Crater3-39">\n         [39]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <i>\n        Curiosity\n       </i>\n       rover is currently probing the environment for past and present\n       <a href="/wiki/Planetary_habitability" title="Planetary habitability">\n        planetary habitability\n       </a>\n       of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Microbe" title="Microbe">\n        microbial\n       </a>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Life_on_Mars_(planet)" title="Life on Mars (planet)">\n        life on Mars\n       </a>\n       . On 9 December 2013, NASA reported that, based on evidence from\n       <i>\n        Curiosity\n       </i>\n       studying\n       <a href="/wiki/Aeolis_Palus" title="Aeolis Palus">\n        Aeolis Palus\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Gale_(crater)" title="Gale (crater)">\n        Gale Crater\n       </a>\n       contained an ancient\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Freshwater_lake" title="Freshwater lake">\n        freshwater lake\n       </a>\n       which could have been a hospitable environment for\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Microbial_life" title="Microbial life">\n        microbial life\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-20131209_40-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NYT-20131209-40">\n         [40]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SCI-20131209_41-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-SCI-20131209-41">\n         [41]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/European_Space_Agency" title="European Space Agency">\n        European Space Agency\n       </a>\n       is currently collaborating with the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_Federal_Space_Agency" title="Russian Federal Space Agency">\n        Russian Federal Space Agency\n       </a>\n       (Roscosmos) and developing the\n       <a href="/wiki/ExoMars" title="ExoMars">\n        ExoMars\n       </a>\n       astrobiology rover, which is to be launched in 2018.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ESA_signed_42-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ESA_signed-42">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Meanwhile, NASA is developing the\n       <a href="/wiki/Mars_2020" title="Mars 2020">\n        Mars 2020\n       </a>\n       astrobiology rover and sample cacher for a later return to Earth.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Methodology">\n        Methodology\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Astrobiology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Methodology">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Planetary_habitability">\n        Planetary habitability\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Astrobiology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Planetary habitability">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Planetary_habitability" title="Planetary habitability">\n        Planetary habitability\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       When looking for life on other planets like Earth, some simplifying assumptions are useful to reduce the size of the task of the astrobiologist. One is the informed assumption that the vast majority of life forms in our galaxy are based on\n       <a href="/wiki/Carbon-based_life" title="Carbon-based life">\n        carbon chemistries\n       </a>\n       , as are all life forms on Earth.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">\n        <a href="#cite_note-43">\n         [43]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Carbon is well known for the unusually wide variety of\n       <a href="/wiki/Molecule" title="Molecule">\n        molecules\n       </a>\n       that can be formed around it. Carbon is the\n       <a href="/wiki/Abundance_of_the_chemical_elements" title="Abundance of the chemical elements">\n        fourth most abundant element\n       </a>\n       in the universe and the energy required to make or break a bond is at just the appropriate level for building molecules which are not only stable, but also reactive. The fact that carbon atoms bond readily to other carbon atoms allows for the building of extremely long and\n       <a href="/wiki/Organic_compound" title="Organic compound">\n        complex molecules\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The presence of liquid water is an assumed requirement, as it is a common molecule and provides an excellent environment for the formation of complicated carbon-based molecules that could eventually lead to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Abiogenesis" title="Abiogenesis">\n        emergence of life\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">\n        <a href="#cite_note-44">\n         [44]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Some researchers posit environments of water-\n       <a href="/wiki/Ammonia" title="Ammonia">\n        ammonia\n       </a>\n       mixtures as possible solvents for\n       <a href="/wiki/Hypothetical_types_of_biochemistry" title="Hypothetical types of biochemistry">\n        hypothetical types of biochemistry\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">\n        <a href="#cite_note-45">\n         [45]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A third assumption is to focus on planets orbiting\n       <a href="/wiki/Sun" title="Sun">\n        Sun\n       </a>\n       -like\n       <a href="/wiki/Star" title="Star">\n        stars\n       </a>\n       for increased probabilities of\n       <a href="/wiki/Planetary_habitability" title="Planetary habitability">\n        planetary habitability\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">\n        <a href="#cite_note-46">\n         [46]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Very large stars have relatively short lifetimes, meaning that life might not have time to emerge on\n       <a href="/wiki/Planet" title="Planet">\n        planets\n       </a>\n       orbiting them. Very small stars provide so little heat and warmth that only planets in very close orbits around them would not be frozen solid, and in such close orbits these planets would be\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tidal_lock" title="Tidal lock">\n        tidally "locked"\n       </a>\n       to the star.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">\n        <a href="#cite_note-47">\n         [47]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The long lifetimes of\n       <a href="/wiki/Red_dwarf" title="Red dwarf">\n        red dwarfs\n       </a>\n       could allow the development of habitable environments on planets with thick atmospheres. This is significant, as red dwarfs are extremely common. (See\n       <a href="/wiki/Habitability_of_red_dwarf_systems" title="Habitability of red dwarf systems">\n        Habitability of red dwarf systems\n       </a>\n       ).\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Since Earth is the only planet known to harbor\n       <a href="/wiki/Life" title="Life">\n        life\n       </a>\n       , there is no evident way to know if any of these simplifying assumptions are correct.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Communication_attempts">\n        Communication attempts\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Astrobiology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Communication attempts">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Communication_with_extraterrestrial_intelligence" title="Communication with extraterrestrial intelligence">\n        Communication with extraterrestrial intelligence\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pioneer10-plaque_tilt.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2246" data-file-width="2856" height="173" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Pioneer10-plaque_tilt.jpg/220px-Pioneer10-plaque_tilt.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Pioneer10-plaque_tilt.jpg/330px-Pioneer10-plaque_tilt.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Pioneer10-plaque_tilt.jpg/440px-Pioneer10-plaque_tilt.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pioneer10-plaque_tilt.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The illustration on the\n         <a href="/wiki/Pioneer_plaque" title="Pioneer plaque">\n          Pioneer plaque\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Research on communication with extraterrestrial intelligence (\n       <a href="/wiki/Communication_with_extraterrestrial_intelligence" title="Communication with extraterrestrial intelligence">\n        CETI\n       </a>\n       ) focuses on composing and deciphering messages that could theoretically be understood by another technological civilization. Communication attempts by humans have included broadcasting mathematical languages, pictorial systems such as the\n       <a href="/wiki/Arecibo_message" title="Arecibo message">\n        Arecibo message\n       </a>\n       and computational approaches to detecting and deciphering \'natural\' language communication. The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SETI" title="SETI">\n        SETI\n       </a>\n       program, for example, uses both\n       <a href="/wiki/Radio_telescope" title="Radio telescope">\n        radio telescopes\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Optical_telescope" title="Optical telescope">\n        optical telescopes\n       </a>\n       to search for deliberate signals from an\n       <a href="/wiki/Extraterrestrial_intelligence" title="Extraterrestrial intelligence">\n        extraterrestrial intelligence\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       While some high-profile scientists, such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Carl_Sagan" title="Carl Sagan">\n        Carl Sagan\n       </a>\n       , have advocated the transmission of messages,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">\n        <a href="#cite_note-48">\n         [48]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">\n        <a href="#cite_note-49">\n         [49]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       scientist\n       <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Hawking" title="Stephen Hawking">\n        Stephen Hawking\n       </a>\n       has warned against it, suggesting that aliens might simply raid Earth for its resources and then move on.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">\n        <a href="#cite_note-50">\n         [50]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Elements_of_astrobiology">\n        Elements of astrobiology\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Astrobiology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Elements of astrobiology">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Astronomy">\n        Astronomy\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Astrobiology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Astronomy">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Astronomy" title="Astronomy">\n        Astronomy\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:OGLE-2005-BLG-390Lb_planet.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="960" data-file-width="1280" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/OGLE-2005-BLG-390Lb_planet.jpg/200px-OGLE-2005-BLG-390Lb_planet.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/OGLE-2005-BLG-390Lb_planet.jpg/300px-OGLE-2005-BLG-390Lb_planet.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/OGLE-2005-BLG-390Lb_planet.jpg/400px-OGLE-2005-BLG-390Lb_planet.jpg 2x" width="200"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:OGLE-2005-BLG-390Lb_planet.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Artist\'s impression of the\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extrasolar_planet" title="Extrasolar planet">\n          extrasolar planet\n         </a>\n         <a href="/wiki/OGLE-2005-BLG-390Lb" title="OGLE-2005-BLG-390Lb">\n          OGLE-2005-BLG-390Lb\n         </a>\n         orbiting its star 20,000\n         <a href="/wiki/Light-year" title="Light-year">\n          light-years\n         </a>\n         from\n         <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">\n          Earth\n         </a>\n         ; this planet was discovered with\n         <a href="/wiki/Gravitational_microlensing" title="Gravitational microlensing">\n          gravitational microlensing\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Telescope_Kepler-NASA.jpeg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="591" data-file-width="864" height="137" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Telescope_Kepler-NASA.jpeg/200px-Telescope_Kepler-NASA.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Telescope_Kepler-NASA.jpeg/300px-Telescope_Kepler-NASA.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Telescope_Kepler-NASA.jpeg/400px-Telescope_Kepler-NASA.jpeg 2x" width="200"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Telescope_Kepler-NASA.jpeg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The\n         <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">\n          NASA\n         </a>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kepler_mission" title="Kepler mission">\n          Kepler mission\n         </a>\n         , launched in March 2009, searches for\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extrasolar_planets" title="Extrasolar planets">\n          extrasolar planets\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Most astronomy-related astrobiology research falls into the category of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extrasolar_planet" title="Extrasolar planet">\n        extrasolar planet\n       </a>\n       (exoplanet) detection, the hypothesis being that if life arose on Earth, then it could also arise on other planets with similar characteristics. To that end, a number of instruments designed to detect Earth-sized exoplanets have been considered, most notably\n       <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">\n        NASA\n       </a>\n       \'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Terrestrial_Planet_Finder" title="Terrestrial Planet Finder">\n        Terrestrial Planet Finder\n       </a>\n       (TPF) and\n       <a href="/wiki/European_Space_Agency" title="European Space Agency">\n        ESA\'s\n       </a>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Darwin_(ESA)" title="Darwin (ESA)">\n        Darwin\n       </a>\n       programs, both of which have been cancelled. NASA launched the\n       <a href="/wiki/Kepler_(spacecraft)" title="Kepler (spacecraft)">\n        <i>\n         Kepler\n        </i>\n        mission\n       </a>\n       in March 2009, and the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_Space_Agency" title="French Space Agency">\n        French Space Agency\n       </a>\n       launched the\n       <a href="/wiki/COROT" title="COROT">\n        COROT\n       </a>\n       space mission in 2006.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">\n        <a href="#cite_note-51">\n         [51]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">\n        <a href="#cite_note-52">\n         [52]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       There are also several less ambitious ground-based efforts underway.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The goal of these missions is not only to detect Earth-sized planets, but also to directly detect light from the planet so that it may be studied\n       <a href="/wiki/Spectroscopy" title="Spectroscopy">\n        spectroscopically\n       </a>\n       . By examining planetary spectra, it would be possible to determine the basic composition of an extrasolar planet\'s atmosphere and/or surface. Given this knowledge, it may be possible to assess the likelihood of life being found on that planet. A NASA research group, the Virtual Planet Laboratory,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">\n        <a href="#cite_note-53">\n         [53]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       is using computer modeling to generate a wide variety of virtual planets to see what they would look like if viewed by TPF or Darwin. It is hoped that once these missions come online, their spectra can be cross-checked with these virtual planetary spectra for features that might indicate the presence of life.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       An estimate for the number of planets with intelligent\n       <i>\n        communicative\n       </i>\n       <a href="/wiki/Extraterrestrial_life" title="Extraterrestrial life">\n        extraterrestrial life\n       </a>\n       can be gleaned from the\n       <a href="/wiki/Drake_equation" title="Drake equation">\n        Drake equation\n       </a>\n       , essentially an equation expressing the probability of intelligent life as the product of factors such as the fraction of planets that might be habitable and the fraction of planets on which life might arise:\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">\n        <a href="#cite_note-54">\n         [54]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n          <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n           <semantics>\n            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n              <mi>\n               N\n              </mi>\n              <mo>\n               =\n              </mo>\n              <msup>\n               <mi>\n                R\n               </mi>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mo>\n                 \xe2\x88\x97\n                 <!-- \xe2\x88\x97 -->\n                </mo>\n               </mrow>\n              </msup>\n              <mtext>\n              </mtext>\n              <mo>\n               \xc3\x97\n               <!-- \xc3\x97 -->\n              </mo>\n              <mtext>\n              </mtext>\n              <msub>\n               <mi>\n                f\n               </mi>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mi>\n                 p\n                </mi>\n               </mrow>\n              </msub>\n              <mtext>\n              </mtext>\n              <mo>\n               \xc3\x97\n               <!-- \xc3\x97 -->\n              </mo>\n              <mtext>\n              </mtext>\n              <msub>\n               <mi>\n                n\n               </mi>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mi>\n                 e\n                </mi>\n               </mrow>\n              </msub>\n              <mtext>\n              </mtext>\n              <mo>\n               \xc3\x97\n               <!-- \xc3\x97 -->\n              </mo>\n              <mtext>\n              </mtext>\n              <msub>\n               <mi>\n                f\n               </mi>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mi>\n                 l\n                </mi>\n               </mrow>\n              </msub>\n              <mtext>\n              </mtext>\n              <mo>\n               \xc3\x97\n               <!-- \xc3\x97 -->\n              </mo>\n              <mtext>\n              </mtext>\n              <msub>\n               <mi>\n                f\n               </mi>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mi>\n                 i\n                </mi>\n               </mrow>\n              </msub>\n              <mtext>\n              </mtext>\n              <mo>\n               \xc3\x97\n               <!-- \xc3\x97 -->\n              </mo>\n              <mtext>\n              </mtext>\n              <msub>\n               <mi>\n                f\n               </mi>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mi>\n                 c\n                </mi>\n               </mrow>\n              </msub>\n              <mtext>\n              </mtext>\n              <mo>\n               \xc3\x97\n               <!-- \xc3\x97 -->\n              </mo>\n              <mtext>\n              </mtext>\n              <mi>\n               L\n              </mi>\n             </mstyle>\n            </mrow>\n            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n             {\\displaystyle N=R^{*}~\\times ~f_{p}~\\times ~n_{e}~\\times ~f_{l}~\\times ~f_{i}~\\times ~f_{c}~\\times ~L}\n            </annotation>\n           </semantics>\n          </math>\n         </span>\n         <img alt="N=R^{*}~\\times ~f_{p}~\\times ~n_{e}~\\times ~f_{l}~\\times ~f_{i}~\\times ~f_{c}~\\times ~L" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ef499c2f687f05bdeca3468d04df354fbb1f825f" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:44.25ex; height:3.009ex;"/>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       where:\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <i>\n         <b>\n          N\n         </b>\n        </i>\n        = The number of communicative civilizations\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <i>\n         <b>\n          R*\n         </b>\n        </i>\n        = The rate of formation of suitable stars (stars such as our Sun)\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <i>\n         <b>\n          f\n          <sub>\n           p\n          </sub>\n         </b>\n        </i>\n        = The fraction of those stars with planets (current evidence indicates that planetary systems may be common for stars like the Sun)\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <i>\n         <b>\n          n\n          <sub>\n           e\n          </sub>\n         </b>\n        </i>\n        = The number of Earth-sized worlds per planetary system\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <i>\n         <b>\n          f\n          <sub>\n           l\n          </sub>\n         </b>\n        </i>\n        = The fraction of those Earth-sized planets where life actually develops\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <i>\n         <b>\n          f\n          <sub>\n           i\n          </sub>\n         </b>\n        </i>\n        = The fraction of life sites where intelligence develops\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <i>\n         <b>\n          f\n          <sub>\n           c\n          </sub>\n         </b>\n        </i>\n        = The fraction of communicative planets (those on which electromagnetic communications technology develops)\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <i>\n         <b>\n          L\n         </b>\n        </i>\n        = The "lifetime" of communicating civilizations\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <p>\n       However, whilst the rationale behind the equation is sound, it is unlikely that the equation will be constrained to reasonable limits of error any time soon. The problem with the formula is that it is not usable to generate or support\n       <a href="/wiki/Hypothesis" title="Hypothesis">\n        hypotheses\n       </a>\n       because it contains factors that can never be verified. The first term,\n       <i>\n        <b>\n         R*\n        </b>\n       </i>\n       , number of stars, is generally constrained within a few orders of magnitude. The second and third terms,\n       <i>\n        f\n        <sub>\n         p\n        </sub>\n       </i>\n       , stars with planets and\n       <i>\n        f\n        <sub>\n         e\n        </sub>\n       </i>\n       , planets with habitable conditions, are being evaluated for the star\'s neighborhood. Drake originally formulated the equation merely as an agenda for discussion at the Green Bank conference,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">\n        <a href="#cite_note-55">\n         [55]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       but some applications of the formula had been taken literally and related to simplistic or\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pseudoscientific" title="Pseudoscientific">\n        pseudoscientific\n       </a>\n       arguments.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BC_56-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-BC-56">\n         [56]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Another associated topic is the\n       <a href="/wiki/Fermi_paradox" title="Fermi paradox">\n        Fermi paradox\n       </a>\n       , which suggests that if intelligent life is common in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Universe" title="Universe">\n        universe\n       </a>\n       , then there should be obvious signs of it.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Another active research area in astrobiology is\n       <a href="/wiki/Planetary_system" title="Planetary system">\n        planetary system\n       </a>\n       formation. It has been suggested that the peculiarities of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Solar_System" title="Solar System">\n        Solar System\n       </a>\n       (for example, the presence of\n       <a href="/wiki/Jupiter" title="Jupiter">\n        Jupiter\n       </a>\n       as a protective shield)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">\n        <a href="#cite_note-57">\n         [57]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       may have greatly increased the probability of intelligent life arising on our planet.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">\n        <a href="#cite_note-58">\n         [58]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">\n        <a href="#cite_note-59">\n         [59]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Biology">\n        Biology\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Astrobiology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Biology">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Abiogenesis" title="Abiogenesis">\n        Abiogenesis\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Biology" title="Biology">\n        Biology\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Extremophile" title="Extremophile">\n        Extremophile\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Blacksmoker_in_Atlantic_Ocean.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1780" data-file-width="1208" height="295" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Blacksmoker_in_Atlantic_Ocean.jpg/200px-Blacksmoker_in_Atlantic_Ocean.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Blacksmoker_in_Atlantic_Ocean.jpg/300px-Blacksmoker_in_Atlantic_Ocean.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Blacksmoker_in_Atlantic_Ocean.jpg/400px-Blacksmoker_in_Atlantic_Ocean.jpg 2x" width="200"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Blacksmoker_in_Atlantic_Ocean.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Hydrothermal_vent" title="Hydrothermal vent">\n          Hydrothermal vents\n         </a>\n         are able to support\n         <a href="/wiki/Extremophile" title="Extremophile">\n          extremophile bacteria\n         </a>\n         on\n         <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">\n          Earth\n         </a>\n         and may also support life in other parts of the cosmos.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Biology cannot state that a process or phenomenon, by being mathematically possible, has to exist forcibly in an extraterrestrial body. Biologists specify what is speculative and what is not.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BC_56-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-BC-56">\n         [56]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Until the 1970s,\n       <a href="/wiki/Life" title="Life">\n        life\n       </a>\n       was thought to be entirely dependent on energy from the\n       <a href="/wiki/Sun" title="Sun">\n        Sun\n       </a>\n       . Plants on Earth\'s surface capture energy from\n       <a href="/wiki/Sunlight" title="Sunlight">\n        sunlight\n       </a>\n       to\n       <a href="/wiki/Photosynthesis" title="Photosynthesis">\n        photosynthesize\n       </a>\n       sugars from carbon dioxide and water, releasing oxygen in the process that is then consumed by oxygen-respiring organisms, passing their energy up the\n       <a href="/wiki/Food_chain" title="Food chain">\n        food chain\n       </a>\n       . Even life in the ocean depths, where sunlight cannot reach, was thought to obtain its nourishment either from consuming\n       <a href="/wiki/Marine_snow" title="Marine snow">\n        organic detritus rained down from the surface waters\n       </a>\n       or from eating animals that did.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-smoker_60-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-smoker-60">\n         [60]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The world\'s ability to support life was thought to depend on its access to\n       <a href="/wiki/Sunlight" title="Sunlight">\n        sunlight\n       </a>\n       . However, in 1977, during an exploratory dive to the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Galapagos_Rift" title="Galapagos Rift">\n        Galapagos Rift\n       </a>\n       in the deep-sea exploration submersible\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/DSV_Alvin" title="DSV Alvin">\n         Alvin\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       , scientists discovered colonies of\n       <a href="/wiki/Giant_tube_worm" title="Giant tube worm">\n        giant tube worms\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Clam" title="Clam">\n        clams\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Crustacean" title="Crustacean">\n        crustaceans\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Mussel" title="Mussel">\n        mussels\n       </a>\n       , and other assorted creatures clustered around undersea volcanic features known as\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Black_smoker" title="Black smoker">\n        black smokers\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-smoker_60-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-smoker-60">\n         [60]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       These creatures thrive despite having no access to sunlight, and it was soon discovered that they comprise an entirely independent\n       <a href="/wiki/Ecosystem" title="Ecosystem">\n        ecosystem\n       </a>\n       . Although most of these multicellular lifeforms need dissolved oxygen (produced by oxygenic photosynthesis) for their aerobic cellular respiration and thus are not completely independent from sunlight by themselves, the basis for their food chain is a form of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bacterium" title="Bacterium">\n        bacterium\n       </a>\n       that derives its energy from\n       <a href="/wiki/Redox" title="Redox">\n        oxidization\n       </a>\n       of reactive chemicals, such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen" title="Hydrogen">\n        hydrogen\n       </a>\n       or\n       <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen_sulfide" title="Hydrogen sulfide">\n        hydrogen sulfide\n       </a>\n       , that bubble up from the Earth\'s interior. Other lifeforms entirely decoupled from the energy from sunlight are green sulphur bacteria which are capturing geothermal light for anoxygenic photosynthesis or bacteria running chemolithoautotrophy based on the radioactive decay of uranium.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Trixler2013_61-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Trixler2013-61">\n         [61]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This\n       <a href="/wiki/Chemosynthesis" title="Chemosynthesis">\n        chemosynthesis\n       </a>\n       revolutionized the study of biology and astrobiology by revealing that life need not be sun-dependent; it only requires water and an energy gradient in order to exist.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extremophiles" title="Extremophiles">\n        Extremophiles\n       </a>\n       , organisms able to survive in extreme environments, are a core research element for astrobiologists. Such organisms include\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biota_(ecology)" title="Biota (ecology)">\n        biota\n       </a>\n       which are able to survive several kilometers below the ocean\'s surface near\n       <a href="/wiki/Hydrothermal_vent" title="Hydrothermal vent">\n        hydrothermal vents\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Microbe" title="Microbe">\n        microbes\n       </a>\n       that thrive in highly acidic environments.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">\n        <a href="#cite_note-62">\n         [62]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It is now known that extremophiles thrive in ice, boiling water, acid, alkali, the water core of nuclear reactors, salt crystals, toxic waste and in a range of other extreme habitats that were previously thought to be inhospitable for life.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cavicchioli_63-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Cavicchioli-63">\n         [63]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This opened up a new avenue in astrobiology by massively expanding the number of possible extraterrestrial habitats. Characterization of these organisms, their environments and their evolutionary pathways, is considered a crucial component to understanding how life might evolve elsewhere in the universe. For example, some organisms able to withstand exposure to the vacuum and radiation of outer space include the lichen fungi\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Rhizocarpon_geographicum" title="Rhizocarpon geographicum">\n         Rhizocarpon geographicum\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       and\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Xanthoria_elegans" title="Xanthoria elegans">\n         Xanthoria elegans\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">\n        <a href="#cite_note-64">\n         [64]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       the bacterium\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Bacillus_safensis" title="Bacillus safensis">\n         Bacillus safensis\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ThePlanetaryReport_65-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ThePlanetaryReport-65">\n         [65]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Deinococcus_radiodurans" title="Deinococcus radiodurans">\n         Deinococcus radiodurans\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ThePlanetaryReport_65-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ThePlanetaryReport-65">\n         [65]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Bacillus_subtilis" title="Bacillus subtilis">\n         Bacillus subtilis\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ThePlanetaryReport_65-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ThePlanetaryReport-65">\n         [65]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       yeast\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Saccharomyces_cerevisiae" title="Saccharomyces cerevisiae">\n         Saccharomyces cerevisiae\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ThePlanetaryReport_65-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ThePlanetaryReport-65">\n         [65]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       seeds from\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Arabidopsis_thaliana" title="Arabidopsis thaliana">\n         Arabidopsis thaliana\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       (\'mouse-ear cress\'),\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ThePlanetaryReport_65-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ThePlanetaryReport-65">\n         [65]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       as well as the invertebrate animal\n       <a href="/wiki/Tardigrade" title="Tardigrade">\n        Tardigrade\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ThePlanetaryReport_65-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ThePlanetaryReport-65">\n         [65]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Jupiter\'s moon,\n       <a href="/wiki/Europa_(moon)" title="Europa (moon)">\n        Europa\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cavicchioli_63-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Cavicchioli-63">\n         [63]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">\n        <a href="#cite_note-66">\n         [66]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-galileo_67-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-galileo-67">\n         [67]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">\n        <a href="#cite_note-68">\n         [68]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">\n        <a href="#cite_note-69">\n         [69]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">\n        <a href="#cite_note-70">\n         [70]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and Saturn\'s moon,\n       <a href="/wiki/Enceladus" title="Enceladus">\n        Enceladus\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">\n        <a href="#cite_note-71">\n         [71]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kazan_72-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Kazan-72">\n         [72]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       are now considered the most likely locations for extant extraterrestrial life in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Solar_System" title="Solar System">\n        Solar System\n       </a>\n       due to their\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Subsurface_ocean#Extraterrestrial_oceans" title="Subsurface ocean">\n        subsurface water oceans\n       </a>\n       where radiogenic and tidal heating enables liquid water to exist.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Trixler2013_61-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Trixler2013-61">\n         [61]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The origin of life, known as\n       <a href="/wiki/Abiogenesis" title="Abiogenesis">\n        abiogenesis\n       </a>\n       , distinct from the\n       <a href="/wiki/Evolution#Evolution_of_life" title="Evolution">\n        evolution of life\n       </a>\n       , is another ongoing field of research.\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oparin" title="Oparin">\n        Oparin\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/J._B._S._Haldane" title="J. B. S. Haldane">\n        Haldane\n       </a>\n       postulated that the conditions on the early Earth were conducive to the formation of\n       <a href="/wiki/Organic_compound" title="Organic compound">\n        organic compounds\n       </a>\n       from\n       <a href="/wiki/Inorganic_chemistry" title="Inorganic chemistry">\n        inorganic elements\n       </a>\n       and thus to the formation of many of the chemicals common to all forms of life we see today. The study of this process, known as prebiotic chemistry, has made some progress, but it is still unclear whether or not life could have formed in such a manner on Earth. The alternative hypothesis of\n       <a href="/wiki/Panspermia" title="Panspermia">\n        panspermia\n       </a>\n       is that the first elements of life may have formed on another planet with even more favorable conditions (or even in interstellar space, asteroids, etc.) and then have been carried over to Earth\xe2\x80\x94the\n       <a href="/wiki/Panspermia" title="Panspermia">\n        panspermia\n       </a>\n       hypothesis.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Cosmic_dust" title="Cosmic dust">\n        cosmic dust\n       </a>\n       permeating the universe contains complex\n       <a href="/wiki/Organic_compound" title="Organic compound">\n        organic\n       </a>\n       compounds ("amorphous organic solids with a mixed\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aromatic" title="Aromatic">\n        aromatic\n       </a>\n       -\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aliphatic" title="Aliphatic">\n        aliphatic\n       </a>\n       structure") that could be created naturally, and rapidly, by\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stars" title="Stars">\n        stars\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Space-20111026_73-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Space-20111026-73">\n         [73]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ScienceDaily-20111026_74-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ScienceDaily-20111026-74">\n         [74]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nature-20111026_75-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Nature-20111026-75">\n         [75]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Further, a scientist suggested that these compounds may have been related to the development of life on Earth and said that, "If this is the case, life on Earth may have had an easier time getting started as these organics can serve as basic ingredients for life."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Space-20111026_73-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Space-20111026-73">\n         [73]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In September 2012, NASA
