scientists reported that\n       <a href="/wiki/Polycyclic_aromatic_hydrocarbon" title="Polycyclic aromatic hydrocarbon">\n        polycyclic aromatic hydrocarbons (PAHs)\n       </a>\n       , subjected to\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstellar_medium" title="Interstellar medium">\n        interstellar medium\n       </a>\n       conditions, are transformed through\n       <a href="/wiki/Hydrogenation" title="Hydrogenation">\n        hydrogenation\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Oxygenation_(environmental)" title="Oxygenation (environmental)">\n        oxygenation\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Hydroxylation" title="Hydroxylation">\n        hydroxylation\n       </a>\n       , to more complex\n       <a href="/wiki/Organic_compound" title="Organic compound">\n        organics\n       </a>\n       \xe2\x80\x93 "a step along the path toward\n       <a href="/wiki/Amino_acid" title="Amino acid">\n        amino acids\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Nucleotide" title="Nucleotide">\n        nucleotides\n       </a>\n       , the raw materials of\n       <a href="/wiki/Protein" title="Protein">\n        proteins\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/DNA" title="DNA">\n        DNA\n       </a>\n       , respectively".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Space-20120920_76-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Space-20120920-76">\n         [76]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AJL-20120901_77-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-AJL-20120901-77">\n         [77]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       More than 20% of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Carbon" title="Carbon">\n        carbon\n       </a>\n       in the universe may be associated with PAHs, possible\n       <a href="/wiki/PAH_world_hypothesis" title="PAH world hypothesis">\n        starting materials\n       </a>\n       for the\n       <a href="/wiki/Abiogenesis#PAH_world_hypothesis" title="Abiogenesis">\n        formation\n       </a>\n       of\n       <a href="/wiki/Life#Extraterrestrial_life" title="Life">\n        life\n       </a>\n       . PAHs seem to have been formed shortly after the\n       <a href="/wiki/Big_Bang" title="Big Bang">\n        Big Bang\n       </a>\n       , are widespread throughout the universe, and are associated with\n       <a href="/wiki/Star_formation" title="Star formation">\n        new stars\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exoplanets" title="Exoplanets">\n        exoplanets\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA-20140221_78-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NASA-20140221-78">\n         [78]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Astroecology">\n        Astroecology\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Astrobiology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Astroecology">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Astroecology" title="Astroecology">\n        Astroecology\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Astroecology" title="Astroecology">\n        Astroecology\n       </a>\n       concerns the interactions of life with space environments and resources, in\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Planets" title="Planets">\n        planets\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asteroids" title="Asteroids">\n        asteroids\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Comets" title="Comets">\n        comets\n       </a>\n       . On a larger scale, astroecology concerns resources for life about\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stars" title="Stars">\n        stars\n       </a>\n       in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Galaxy" title="Galaxy">\n        galaxy\n       </a>\n       through the cosmological future. Astroecology attempts to quantify future life in space, addressing this area of astrobiology.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Experimental astroecology investigates resources in planetary soils, using actual space materials in\n       <a href="/wiki/Meteorite" title="Meteorite">\n        meteorites\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AstroecologyIcarus2002_79-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-AstroecologyIcarus2002-79">\n         [79]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The results suggest that Martian and carbonaceous chondrite materials can support\n       <a href="/wiki/Bacteria" title="Bacteria">\n        bacteria\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Algae" title="Algae">\n        algae\n       </a>\n       and plant (asparagus, potato) cultures, with high soil fertilities. The results support that life could have survived in early aqueous asteroids and on similar materials imported to Earth by dust, comets and meteorites, and that such asteroid materials can be used as soil for future space colonies.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AstroecologyIcarus2002_79-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-AstroecologyIcarus2002-79">\n         [79]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AstroecologyAstrobiology2002_80-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-AstroecologyAstrobiology2002-80">\n         [80]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On the largest scale, cosmoecology concerns life in the universe over cosmological times. The main sources of energy may be red giant stars and white and red dwarf stars, sustaining life for 10\n       <sup>\n        20\n       </sup>\n       years.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AstroecologyIcarus2002_79-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-AstroecologyIcarus2002-79">\n         [79]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AstroecologyIcarus2002_79-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-AstroecologyIcarus2002-79">\n         [79]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AstroecologyJBIS2005_81-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-AstroecologyJBIS2005-81">\n         [81]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Astroecologists suggest that their mathematical models may quantify the potential amounts of future life in space, allowing a comparable expansion in biodiversity, potentially leading to diverse intelligent life forms.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">\n        <a href="#cite_note-82">\n         [82]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Astrogeology">\n        Astrogeology\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Astrobiology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Astrogeology">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Geology_of_solar_terrestrial_planets" title="Geology of solar terrestrial planets">\n        Geology of solar terrestrial planets\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Geology_of_solar_terrestrial_planets" title="Geology of solar terrestrial planets">\n        Astrogeology\n       </a>\n       is a\n       <a href="/wiki/Planetary_science" title="Planetary science">\n        planetary science\n       </a>\n       discipline concerned with the\n       <a href="/wiki/Geology" title="Geology">\n        geology\n       </a>\n       of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Celestial_bodies" title="Celestial bodies">\n        celestial bodies\n       </a>\n       such as the\n       <a href="/wiki/Planet" title="Planet">\n        planets\n       </a>\n       and their\n       <a href="/wiki/Moon" title="Moon">\n        moons\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Asteroid" title="Asteroid">\n        asteroids\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Comet" title="Comet">\n        comets\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Meteorite" title="Meteorite">\n        meteorites\n       </a>\n       . The information gathered by this discipline allows the measure of a\n       <a href="/wiki/Planet" title="Planet">\n        planet\n       </a>\n       \'s or a\n       <a href="/wiki/Natural_satellite" title="Natural satellite">\n        natural satellite\n       </a>\n       \'s potential to develop and sustain\n       <a href="/wiki/Life" title="Life">\n        life\n       </a>\n       , or\n       <a href="/wiki/Planetary_habitability" title="Planetary habitability">\n        planetary habitability\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       An additional discipline of astrogeology is\n       <a href="/wiki/Geochemistry" title="Geochemistry">\n        geochemistry\n       </a>\n       , which involves study of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Chemistry" title="Chemistry">\n        chemical\n       </a>\n       composition of the Earth and other\n       <a href="/wiki/Planet" title="Planet">\n        planets\n       </a>\n       , chemical processes and reactions that govern the composition of\n       <a href="/wiki/Rock_(geology)" title="Rock (geology)">\n        rocks\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Soil" title="Soil">\n        soils\n       </a>\n       , the cycles of matter and energy and their interaction with the\n       <a href="/wiki/Hydrosphere" title="Hydrosphere">\n        hydrosphere\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Atmosphere" title="Atmosphere">\n        atmosphere\n       </a>\n       of the planet. Specializations include\n       <a href="/wiki/Cosmochemistry" title="Cosmochemistry">\n        cosmochemistry\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Biochemistry" title="Biochemistry">\n        biochemistry\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Organic_geochemistry" title="Organic geochemistry">\n        organic geochemistry\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fossil_record" title="Fossil record">\n        fossil record\n       </a>\n       provides the oldest known evidence for life on Earth.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">\n        <a href="#cite_note-83">\n         [83]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       By examining the fossil evidence,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paleontologists" title="Paleontologists">\n        paleontologists\n       </a>\n       are able to better understand the types of organisms that arose on the early Earth. Some regions on Earth, such as the\n       <a href="/wiki/Pilbara" title="Pilbara">\n        Pilbara\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Western_Australia" title="Western Australia">\n        Western Australia\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/McMurdo_Dry_Valleys" title="McMurdo Dry Valleys">\n        McMurdo Dry Valleys\n       </a>\n       of Antarctica, are also considered to be geological analogs to regions of Mars, and as such, might be able to provide clues on how to search for past\n       <a href="/wiki/Life_on_Mars" title="Life on Mars">\n        life on Mars\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The various organic functional groups, composed of hydrogen, oxygen, nitrogen, phosphorus, sulfur, and a host of metals, such as iron, magnesium, and zinc, provide the enormous diversity of chemical reactions necessarily catalyzed by a living\n       <a href="/wiki/Organism" title="Organism">\n        organism\n       </a>\n       . Silicon, in contrast, interacts with only a few other atoms, and the large silicon molecules are monotonous compared with the combinatorial universe of organic macromolecules.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BC_56-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-BC-56">\n         [56]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pace_84-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Pace-84">\n         [84]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Indeed, it seems likely that the basic building blocks of life anywhere will be similar those on Earth, in the generality if not in the detail.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pace_84-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Pace-84">\n         [84]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Although terrestrial life and life that might arise independently of Earth are expected to use many similar, if not identical, building blocks, they also are expected to have some biochemical qualities that are unique. If life has had a comparable impact elsewhere in the Solar System, the relative abundances of chemicals key for its survival \xe2\x80\x93 whatever they may be \xe2\x80\x93 could betray its presence. Whatever extraterrestrial life may be, its tendency to chemically alter its environment might just give it away.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">\n        <a href="#cite_note-85">\n         [85]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Life_in_the_Solar_System">\n        Life in the Solar System\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Astrobiology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Life in the Solar System">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Abiogenesis" title="Abiogenesis">\n        Abiogenesis\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Life_on_Mars" title="Life on Mars">\n        Life on Mars\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Life_on_Europa" title="Life on Europa">\n        Life on Europa\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Life_on_Titan" title="Life on Titan">\n        Life on Titan\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Hypothetical_types_of_biochemistry" title="Hypothetical types of biochemistry">\n        Hypothetical types of biochemistry\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PIA01130_Interior_of_Europa.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="2666" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/PIA01130_Interior_of_Europa.jpg/200px-PIA01130_Interior_of_Europa.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/PIA01130_Interior_of_Europa.jpg/300px-PIA01130_Interior_of_Europa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/PIA01130_Interior_of_Europa.jpg/400px-PIA01130_Interior_of_Europa.jpg 2x" width="200"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PIA01130_Interior_of_Europa.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Europa_(moon)" title="Europa (moon)">\n          Europa\n         </a>\n         , due to the ocean that exists under its icy surface, might host some form of\n         <a href="/wiki/Bacteria" title="Bacteria">\n          microbial life\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       People have long speculated about the possibility of life in settings other than Earth, however, speculation on the nature of life elsewhere often has paid little heed to constraints imposed by the nature of biochemistry.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pace_84-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Pace-84">\n         [84]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The likelihood that life throughout the universe is probably carbon-based is suggested by the fact that carbon is one of the most abundant of the higher elements. Only two of the natural atoms,\n       <a href="/wiki/Carbon" title="Carbon">\n        carbon\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Silicon" title="Silicon">\n        silicon\n       </a>\n       , are known to serve as the backbones of molecules sufficiently large to carry biological information. As the structural basis for life, one of carbon\'s important features is that unlike silicon, it can readily engage in the formation of chemical bonds with many other atoms, thereby allowing for the chemical versatility required to conduct the reactions of biological metabolism and propagation.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Thought on where in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Solar_System" title="Solar System">\n        Solar System\n       </a>\n       life might occur, was limited historically by the understanding that life relies ultimately on light and warmth from the Sun and, therefore, is restricted to the surfaces of planets.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pace_84-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Pace-84">\n         [84]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The three most likely candidates for life in the Solar System are the planet\n       <a href="/wiki/Mars" title="Mars">\n        Mars\n       </a>\n       , the Jovian moon\n       <a href="/wiki/Europa_(moon)" title="Europa (moon)">\n        Europa\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Saturn" title="Saturn">\n        Saturn\n       </a>\n       \'s moons\n       <a href="/wiki/Titan_(moon)" title="Titan (moon)">\n        Titan\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Europa_86-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Europa-86">\n         [86]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EuroUpdate_87-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-EuroUpdate-87">\n         [87]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">\n        <a href="#cite_note-88">\n         [88]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">\n        <a href="#cite_note-89">\n         [89]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Titan1_90-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Titan1-90">\n         [90]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Enceladus" title="Enceladus">\n        Enceladus\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kazan_72-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Kazan-72">\n         [72]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lovett_91-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Lovett-91">\n         [91]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Mars" title="Mars">\n        Mars\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Enceladus_(moon)" title="Enceladus (moon)">\n        Enceladus\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Europa_(moon)" title="Europa (moon)">\n        Europa\n       </a>\n       are considered likely candidates in the search for life primarily because they may have underground liquid water, a molecule essential for life as we know it for its use as a\n       <a href="/wiki/Solvent" title="Solvent">\n        solvent\n       </a>\n       in cells.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_34-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-34">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Water on Mars is found frozen in its polar ice caps, and newly carved gullies recently observed on Mars suggest that liquid water may exist, at least transiently, on the planet\'s surface.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">\n        <a href="#cite_note-92">\n         [92]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">\n        <a href="#cite_note-93">\n         [93]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       At the Martian low temperatures and low pressure, liquid water is likely to be highly saline.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">\n        <a href="#cite_note-94">\n         [94]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       As for Europa, liquid water likely exists beneath the moon\'s icy outer crust.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-galileo_67-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-galileo-67">\n         [67]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Europa_86-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Europa-86">\n         [86]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EuroUpdate_87-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-EuroUpdate-87">\n         [87]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This water may be warmed to a liquid state by volcanic vents on the ocean floor, but the primary source of heat is probably\n       <a href="/wiki/Tidal_heating" title="Tidal heating">\n        tidal heating\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">\n        <a href="#cite_note-95">\n         [95]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       On 11 December 2013, NASA reported the detection of "\n       <a href="/wiki/Clay_minerals" title="Clay minerals">\n        clay-like minerals\n       </a>\n       " (specifically,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Phyllosilicates" title="Phyllosilicates">\n        phyllosilicates\n       </a>\n       ), often associated with\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Organic_materials" title="Organic materials">\n        organic materials\n       </a>\n       , on the icy crust of\n       <a href="/wiki/Europa_(moon)" title="Europa (moon)">\n        Europa\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA-20131211_96-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NASA-20131211-96">\n         [96]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The presence of the minerals may have been the result of a collision with an\n       <a href="/wiki/Asteroid" title="Asteroid">\n        asteroid\n       </a>\n       or\n       <a href="/wiki/Comet" title="Comet">\n        comet\n       </a>\n       according to the scientists.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA-20131211_96-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NASA-20131211-96">\n         [96]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Another\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_planetary_bodies" title="List of planetary bodies">\n        planetary body\n       </a>\n       that could potentially sustain extraterrestrial life is\n       <a href="/wiki/Saturn" title="Saturn">\n        Saturn\n       </a>\n       \'s largest moon,\n       <a href="/wiki/Titan_(moon)" title="Titan (moon)">\n        Titan\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Titan1_90-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Titan1-90">\n         [90]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Titan has been described as having conditions similar to those of early\n       <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">\n        Earth\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">\n        <a href="#cite_note-97">\n         [97]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       On its surface, scientists have discovered the first liquid lakes outside Earth, but these lakes seem to be composed of\n       <a href="/wiki/Ethane" title="Ethane">\n        ethane\n       </a>\n       and/or\n       <a href="/wiki/Methane" title="Methane">\n        methane\n       </a>\n       , not water.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">\n        <a href="#cite_note-98">\n         [98]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Some scientists think it possible that these liquid\n       <a href="/wiki/Hydrocarbon" title="Hydrocarbon">\n        hydrocarbons\n       </a>\n       might take the place of water in\n       <a href="/wiki/Hypothetical_types_of_biochemistry" title="Hypothetical types of biochemistry">\n        living cells different from those on Earth\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">\n        <a href="#cite_note-99">\n         [99]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">\n        <a href="#cite_note-100">\n         [100]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       After Cassini data was studied, it was reported on March 2008 that Titan may also have an underground ocean composed of liquid\n       <a href="/wiki/Water" title="Water">\n        water\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Ammonia" title="Ammonia">\n        ammonia\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101">\n        <a href="#cite_note-101">\n         [101]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Additionally, Saturn\'s moon\n       <a href="/wiki/Enceladus" title="Enceladus">\n        Enceladus\n       </a>\n       may have an ocean below its icy surface\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">\n        <a href="#cite_note-102">\n         [102]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and, according to NASA scientists in May 2011, "is emerging as the most habitable spot beyond Earth in the Solar System for life as we know it".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kazan_72-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Kazan-72">\n         [72]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lovett_91-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Lovett-91">\n         [91]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Measuring the ratio of\n       <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen" title="Hydrogen">\n        hydrogen\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Methane" title="Methane">\n        methane\n       </a>\n       levels on Mars may help determine the likelihood of\n       <a href="/wiki/Life_on_Mars" title="Life on Mars">\n        life on Mars\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PNAS-20120607_103-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-PNAS-20120607-103">\n         [103]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Space-20120625_104-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Space-20120625-104">\n         [104]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       According to the scientists, "...low H\n       <sub>\n        2\n       </sub>\n       /CH\n       <sub>\n        4\n       </sub>\n       ratios (less than approximately 40) indicate that life is likely present and active."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PNAS-20120607_103-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-PNAS-20120607-103">\n         [103]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Other scientists have recently reported methods of detecting hydrogen and methane in\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extraterrestrial_atmospheres" title="Extraterrestrial atmospheres">\n        extraterrestrial atmospheres\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nature-20120627_105-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Nature-20120627-105">\n         [105]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wired-20120627_106-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Wired-20120627-106">\n         [106]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Complex\n       <a href="/wiki/Organic_compound" title="Organic compound">\n        organic compounds\n       </a>\n       of life, including\n       <a href="/wiki/Uracil" title="Uracil">\n        uracil\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Cytosine" title="Cytosine">\n        cytosine\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Thymine" title="Thymine">\n        thymine\n       </a>\n       , have been formed in a laboratory under\n       <a href="/wiki/Outer_space" title="Outer space">\n        outer space\n       </a>\n       conditions, using starting chemicals such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Pyrimidine" title="Pyrimidine">\n        pyrimidine\n       </a>\n       , found in\n       <a href="/wiki/Meteorite" title="Meteorite">\n        meteorites\n       </a>\n       . Pyrimidine, like\n       <a href="/wiki/Polycyclic_aromatic_hydrocarbon" title="Polycyclic aromatic hydrocarbon">\n        polycyclic aromatic hydrocarbons\n       </a>\n       (PAHs), is the most carbon-rich chemical found in\n       <a href="/wiki/Universe" title="Universe">\n        the universe\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA-20150303_107-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NASA-20150303-107">\n         [107]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Rare_Earth_hypothesis">\n        Rare Earth hypothesis\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Astrobiology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Rare Earth hypothesis">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Rare_Earth_hypothesis" title="Rare Earth hypothesis">\n        Rare Earth hypothesis\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The Rare Earth hypothesis postulates that multicellular life forms found on Earth may actually be more of a rarity than scientists assume. It provides a possible answer to the Fermi paradox which suggests, "If extraterrestrial aliens are common, why aren\'t they obvious?" It is apparently in opposition to the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Principle_of_mediocrity" title="Principle of mediocrity">\n        principle of mediocrity\n       </a>\n       , assumed by famed astronomers\n       <a href="/wiki/Frank_Drake" title="Frank Drake">\n        Frank Drake\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Carl_Sagan" title="Carl Sagan">\n        Carl Sagan\n       </a>\n       , and others. The Principle of Mediocrity suggests that life on Earth is not exceptional, but rather that life is more than likely to be found on innumerable other worlds.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Anthropic_principle" title="Anthropic principle">\n        anthropic principle\n       </a>\n       states that fundamental laws of the universe work specifically in a way that life would be possible. The anthropic principle supports the Rare Earth Hypothesis by arguing the overall elements that are needed to support life on Earth are so fine-tuned that it is nearly impossible for another just like it to exist by random chance.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Research">\n        Research\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Astrobiology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Research">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="toccolours searchaux" id="Container" style="text-align: left; padding:0.5em 0 0 0; border-style:solid; float:right;clear:right; padding:0 0.5em; margin:0.3em 0 0.8em 1.4em; overflow: hidden;">\n       <div id="Title" style="background-color:#77bb77; font-weight:bold; padding:0.2em; text-align:center; margin:0.6em 0 1.2em 0">\n        <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_the_formation_of_the_Universe" title="Timeline of the formation of the Universe">\n         Nature timeline\n        </a>\n       </div>\n       <div id="Contains-Timeline-Scale-Notes">\n        <div style="text-align:right; position:relative; top:-1em;">\n         <small>\n          <a href="/wiki/Template:Nature_timeline" title="Template:Nature timeline">\n           <span style="color:#002bb8;" title="View this timeline in its own page">\n            view\n           </span>\n          </a>\n          \xe2\x80\xa2\n          <a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Nature_timeline" title="Template talk:Nature timeline">\n           <span style="color:#002bb8;" title="Discussion about this template">\n            discuss\n           </span>\n          </a>\n          \xe2\x80\xa2\n          <span class="noprint plainlinksneverexpand" style="color:#002bb8;" title="You can edit this timeline. Please use the preview button before saving.">\n           <span class="plainlinks">\n            <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Nature_timeline&amp;action=edit">\n             edit\n            </a>\n           </span>\n          </span>\n         </small>\n        </div>\n        <div id="Scale" style="width:3.1em; position:relative; top:-0.82em; float:left; height:36em; padding:0px">\n         <div style="float:right; position:absolute; right:-1px; top:33.91550112327em;">\n          <span style="font-size:86%;white-space:nowrap;">\n           -13\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x94\n          </span>\n         </div>\n         <div style="float:right; position:absolute; right:-1px; top:32.611058772375em;">\n          <span style="font-size:86%;white-space:nowrap;">\n           \xe2\x80\x93\n          </span>\n         </div>\n         <div style="float:right; position:absolute; right:-1px; top:31.30661642148em;">\n          <span style="font-size:86%;white-space:nowrap;">\n           -12\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x94\n          </span>\n         </div>\n         <div style="float:right; position:absolute; right:-1px; top:30.002174070585em;">\n          <span style="font-size:86%;white-space:nowrap;">\n           \xe2\x80\x93\n          </span>\n         </div>\n         <div style="float:right; position:absolute; right:-1px; top:28.69773171969em;">\n          <span style="font-size:86%;white-space:nowrap;">\n           -11\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x94\n          </span>\n         </div>\n         <div style="float:right; position:absolute; right:-1px; top:27.393289368795em;">\n          <span style="font-size:86%;white-space:nowrap;">\n           \xe2\x80\x93\n          </span>\n         </div>\n         <div style="float:right; position:absolute; right:-1px; top:26.0888470179em;">\n          <span style="font-size:86%;white-space:nowrap;">\n           -10\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x94\n          </span>\n         </div>\n         <div style="float:right; position:absolute; right:-1px; top:24.784404667005em;">\n          <span style="font-size:86%;white-space:nowrap;">\n           \xe2\x80\x93\n          </span>\n         </div>\n         <div style="float:right; position:absolute; right:-1px; top:23.47996231611em;">\n          <span style="font-size:86%;white-space:nowrap;">\n           -9\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x94\n          </span>\n         </div>\n         <div style="float:right;
